# Author: Paul Chichura (pchichura@uchicago.edu)
# Date queried: June 22, 2021
# Date updated: September 17, 2021
# 
# This file contains a list of solar system objects with published diameters,
# queried from https://ssd.jpl.nasa.gov/sbdb_query.cgi along with object
# diameter, perihelion distance, and minimum orbit intersection distance.
# These values were used to estimate the brightest an object could be under
# ideal observing geometry using the Standard Thermal Model and assuming
# r_sun=perihelion, r_earth=MOID, phase angle=0, emissivity=1, albedo=0, and
# beaming parameter=0.756. Objects included in this list either have a max
# estimated flux of at least 0.5mJy at 150GHz, are classified as a Near Earth
# Object (NEO), or are a comet. For details of this selection, see:
# https://pole.uchicago.edu/sptpol/index.php/Asteroids
# 
# Note that comet orbits may change due to outgassing near perihelion. In cases
# with multiple apparitions, these objects are treated differently in the table.
# 
# Tab-delimited contents:
# fullname: human-readable name
#     asteroids: "{primary designation} {name} ({provisional designation})"
#     comets: "{primary designation}/{name} {number (if multiple appartitions)}"
# queryname: JPL-HORIZONS-friendly name for querying
#     asteroids: primary des. if available, otherwise provisional des.
#     comets with one app.: primary des.
#     comets with multiple app.: JPL record number of most recent apparition
# type: multi-character string identifying type of object
#     "A": asteroid
#     "P", "C", "D": periodic, non-periodic, or lost comets, respectively
#     "N": NEO
# max_flux_150ghz: maximum possible flux at 150GHz in mJy as described above
# 
# -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
